'Buffy' Star Sarah Michelle Gellar Shares Touching Tribute to Late Anthony Head — 'I'm the Lucky One'
Source: EntertainmentNow    Published: 2026-06-07 00:14:45

Heartbroken actress Sarah Michelle Gellar has shared a touching tribute to English actor Anthony Head, following the sad news of his passing at the age of 72. Gellar, 49, starred as the eponymous Buffy Summers in “Buffy the Vampire Slayer” — the series that many people are most familiar with Head from. Head played Rupert Giles in the show. Giles was the “Watcher” of Buffy Summers. A Watcher is a guardian, mentor, and researcher assigned to train and guide a Vampire Slayer. It was a relationship the two characters maintained (more or less) for all seven seasons and 144 episodes of the show between 1997 and 2003. While Gellar, as the show's star, appeared in all 144 episodes (per IMDb), Head wasn't too far behind, having appeared in 121 (also per IMDb). Gellar took to social media to share her tribute to Head. Sarah Michelle Gellar shared her tribute to Anthony Head with her five million followers on her Instagram account. The post comprises four pictures. The first picture is of Gellar and Seth Green with Head and his two daughters. The second is of Gellar and her husband, Freddie Prinze Jr., with Head. The third is of Gellar and her daughter, Charlotte Grace Prinze, with Head. The fourth is a still from a “Buffy the Vampire Slayer” scene in which Head's Giles humorously lies to Gellar's Buffy about how easy life is. Gellar captioned her post, “”Tell Giles I figured it out and I'm ok””” Well I don't have it figured out and I'm not ok. But I know I'm the lucky one because I knew you. Thank you to Daisy and Emily who not only shared their dad with me, but with the world.” The “Tell Giles I figured it out and I'm ok” line is from season five of “Buffy the Vampire Slayer,” when Buffy leaves a message for her Watcher after deciding to sacrifice herself to save the world. It was a poignant call-back to Gellar's time working with Head. Gellar's followers flocked en masse to the comments section of her post to pay their own respects to Head and offer comfort to the actress. The comments on Sarah Michelle Gellar's tribute to Anthony Head were all lovely. One of the followers commented, “If there's one thing for certain, it's that the Buffy family will be there to comfort one another through this heart ache the way we always know how ❤️🫂.” Another one said, “I'm so sorry for your loss Sarah. You and Anthony shared such a beautiful special Father Daughter relationship on-screen. I will always remember his iconic moments like “Cooper's got a gun” and the love and warmth he brought to the Buffyverse 💝.” Someone else wrote, “Im so sorry for your loss 🤍 He helped all of us grow up.” Finally, one Instagram user noted, “I am so sorry, Sarah. You have lost so many people over the last couple of years. Much love to you at this time.” The last user was, of course, referring to the fact that two other “Buffy the Vampire Slayer” stars have passed since the start of 2025. Michelle Trachtenberg, who played Buffy's sister Dawn, and Nicholas Brendon, who played Buffy's friend Xander Harris, have both sadly departed this mortal coil recently. We'd like to send our heartfelt condolences to all of Anthony Head's friends and loved ones. May he rest in eternal peace. Like EntertainmentNow? OTHER

United States Declassifies Documents About UFOs, but Nothing Conclusive Yet
Source: ColombiaOne.com    Published: 2026-06-07 01:00:00

- The announcement has been more sensationalist and far less revealing. The United States Department of Defense began this Friday to comply with President Donald Trump's order to disclose documents held by the US government containing information on Unidentified Aerial Phenomena (UAP). Although the move reignited a debate that opened back in the 1940s and gave wings to those who defend the idea of extraterrestrial life, so far there has been no surprising revelation about the existence of aliens, and even less any conclusive evidence. Thus, this Friday dozens of PDF documents, videos and images labeled with the attractive description “never seen before” were released to the public, a label that will always attract curiosity. All of this is enriching the website war.gov/ufo, which will be updated each week with new material. The website features a retro design concept within the technological world, highlighting white text on an overwhelming black background. The shock for the more skeptical has been to encounter blurry photographs that say nothing about the enigmatic and elusive extraterrestrials. The site war.gov/ufo launched with 161 items, including diplomatic cables, interviews with witnesses describing alleged encounters with UAP, and images captured on film during the Apollo 12 (1969) and Apollo 17 (1972) space missions. It also includes photographs taken from the Moon during that last mission, never seen before, as well as transcripts of communications between the spacecraft's pilots. The publication of these documents had been announced by President Trump last February on his social network Truth. There he expressed his desire to release materials such as those published this Friday. “In view of the great interest shown, I will direct the Secretary of War [Pete Hegseth] and other relevant departments and agencies to begin the process of identifying and releasing government files related to extraterrestrial life, unidentified aerial phenomena and unidentified flying objects, as well as any other information related to these highly complex but extremely interesting and important matters,” he wrote at the time. And this Friday, the US president, on the same social network, defended the publication of the documents. He said it is “an effort to achieve total and maximum transparency.” In an additional comment, he sought to draw people's attention, but also made it clear that he has not seen anything he finds particularly surprising. “With these new documents and videos, people can decide for themselves: ‘WHAT THE HELL IS GOING ON?'. Have fun and enjoy!” he wrote, as if promoting a movie or television program. The process of publishing these documents was accelerated after an exchange of statements with Barack Obama, who had said in a podcast that these phenomena “are real,” although he denied having evidence of secret installations. The world was shaken by this statement from the former president, and Trump accused him of revealing classified information. For that reason, he decided to move ahead by publishing the entire catalog in order to demonstrate the supposed “total transparency” of his administration. The publication of the documents is also seen by Trump's critics as a smokescreen to distract public attention at a time when the president is recording very low approval ratings, breaking historic lows, due, among other things, to the already prolonged war against Iran, which he promised to end within weeks but which has continued with dangerous consequences not only for the United States (including rising gasoline prices), but also for the global economy. It also coincides with the lunar mission of the Artemis II spacecraft, which once again placed the United States at the forefront of the space race and reignited enthusiasm for space-related topics. Those who believe in aliens will find in the war.gov/ufo site reasons and clues to reaffirm their convictions. On the contrary, skeptics will continue waiting for that image, that unmistakably clear video, which proves the existence of life in outer space. Biden admin used $500,000 missile to shoot down ‘UFO'—that turned out to be Boy Scouts balloon
Source: AOL.com    Published: 2026-06-07 00:57:15

Advertisement For premium support please call: For premium support please call: The Biden administration obliterated a boy scout balloon with a $500,000 missile in the wake of their bungled response to the Chinese Spy balloon incident, The Post can reveal. The US Air Force dispatched an F-16 on Feb. 12, 2023 to confront the apparent "invading" orb over Lake Huron, blowing it to smithereens with what was likely an AIM-9 Sidewinder missile, according to video released last month by the Department of War as part of its second batch of UFO files. The 45-second clip shows a black "orb" with a dangling string in the fighter jet's crosshairs for just a few seconds before it is blown apart. "The F16 shot at a balloon over Lake Huron. After the [Chinese spy] balloon embarrassment, DOD was shooting at every [Unidentified Anomalous Phenomena] they detected," Tim Phillips, a former interim director of AARO, told The Post. The object belonged to a Boy Scout troop, according to Sean Kirkpatrick, a former head of the federal All-Domain Anomaly Resolution Office, or AARO. "[The balloon] had circumnavigated the globe eight times before we shot it down with a half-million-dollar missile," Kirkpatrick said at a conference on April 27. "You can imagine the response on the Hill when I briefed that," he said at that conference. Advertisement The orb was part of an ongoing, unspecified research project, Kirkpatrick added. The destruction of the Boy Scout balloon came a week after the Chinese Spy Balloon debacle, which saw the feckless administration twiddling their thumbs for five days as a CCP recon operation was fully active in the airspace of the USA. The Biden administration wasted more ammunition shooting down another hobbyist balloon on Feb 11, 2023 over Alaska. A US F-22 fired a $439,000 missile at a research balloon which cost $12 and belonged to the Northern Illinois Bottlecap Balloon Brigade, The Guardian reported. On another occasion, a US fighter pilot reported encountering a UFO with "stealth-like capabilities" and was authorized to fire a missile — only to to destroy a star-shaped mylar balloon from Walmart which said "Happy Birthday," according to Kirkpatrick. Many of the supposed UFO videos produced by the military, some of which are being released by the Trump administration, depict standard manmade objects that were misidentified by Reaper drones operators. "They've been on mission and they've got to get back to base to rearm and refuel. And you've got a bored operator looking around. And they pick something up and aren't sure what it is," Phillips said. "We're actually seeing, good reporting coming out of the fleet, coming out of the operation wings and squadrons, where they're willing to report this stuff. And this is part of that outreach where we get our scientists to talk to the Reaper operators and actually go side by side and try to do some education," he said. Advertisement
